fÃªÀ£ÀzÀ°è£À ªÀåQÛ¤μÀ× ªÀÄvÀÄÛ ªÀ¸ÀÄÛ¤μÀ× zÀÈ¶ÖAiÀÄ£ÀÄß ¥Àæw©A©¸ÀÄªÀ «dAiÀÄPÀÄªÀiÁjAiÀÄªÀgÀ PÀªÀ£ÀUÀ¼ÀÄ ¸Á»vÀåPÀ ¸ÉÆ§UÀÄ ªÀÄvÀÄÛ ¥Àæ¸ÁzÀUÀÄtUÀ¼À MAzÀÄ §UÉAiÀÄ C£À£Àå ¸ÀA«Ä±Àæt. G¥ÀzÉÃ±ÁvÀäPÀ ªÀÄvÀÄÛ «¢ü-¤μÉÃzsÁvÀäPÀ MPÀÌuÉUÀ¼ÀÆ C®è°è £ÀÄ¸ÀÄ½zÀÝgÀÆ CªÀ£ÀÄß ¸À»¹PÉÆ¼ÀÄîªÀμÀÄÖ ªÀiÁvÀæ EªÉ- JA§ ¸ÀªÀiÁzsÁ£ÀªÀAvÀÆ EzÉ; ¸ÀAPÀ®£ÀzÀ ¸ÀªÀÄUÀæ ¥ÀjuÁªÀÄPÉÌ H£ÀªÉÃ£À£ÀÆß CªÀÅ vÁgÀªÀÅ.

Beauty, the essential aesthetic quality of the poetry is reflected by author’s pleasing imagery in this collection of poems by Smt. D L Vijayakumari. We see euphony, the melody of words (especially in this beautifully brought-out English Translation) with ambient play of ornamentation.

Her style exhibits clearness in thought, structure and expression, vigour through terseness, restraint in the idea and mood, picturesqeness in vividly describing actions, feelings and objects, striking presentation using abundant elements of antithesis, contrast and choiceness of expression. Critics rightly observe one’s style as “the product of author’s personality, a transparent record of one’s intellectual, spiritual and artistic development”, and it is true here too.

With subjective and objective outlook in life, Vijayakumaari’s poems have a unique blend of literary charm and grace. Readers may observe a gradual growth in the author’s choice of matter, manner and aim of poems and in her reflecting on the ever widening human experience through this medium. Of course, sermonizing and didactic elements might sparingly have crept in at places, which however would not at all mar the beauty of the collection -Shikaripura Harihareswara a note on Dr. D. L. Vijayakumari's `Flower in the Furnace' pp 123

Dr. C. Naganna writes in his "Translator's Note" thus: In translating Dr. Vijayakumari's poems, I have not tried unnecessarily to inject my borrowed vocabulary as an English teacher. I have stuck to the simple and straightforward path traced by the original creations. The poet has worked with limited tools, but she has exhibited careful craftmanship, in that , the poems acquire variety within he narrow framework. I have tried to replicate it in my translation. .. .."-Flower in the furnace, pp. xv
